Use Of Estimates|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an on-going basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories and product purchase commitments, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, property, plant, and equipment, and other contingencies. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

  Use Of Estimates|c-1|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an on-going basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories and product purchase commitments, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, property, plant, and equipment, and other contingencies. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-
  New Accounting Pronouncements Policy Policy Text Block|c-1|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Recently Issued Accounting PronouncementsRecent Accounting Pronouncements Not Yet AdoptedIn November 2023, the Financial Accounting Standards Board, or FASB, issued a new accounting standard to provide for additional disclosures about significant expenses in operating segments. The standard is effective for our annual reporting starting with fiscal year 2025 and for interim period reporting starting in fiscal year 2026 retrospectively. We are currently evaluating the impact of this standard on our Consolidated Financial Statements.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

@CONCEPT: us-gaap:UseOfEstimates
@VALUE: Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an on-going basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories and product purchase commitments, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, property, plant, and equipment, and other contingencies. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.

These formulas can be used to verify data consistency:
- Current Assets + Non-Current Assets = Total Assets
- Current Liabilities + Non-Current Liabilities + Equity = Total Liabilities and Equity
- Gross Profit = Revenue - Cost of Revenue
- Net Income = Revenue - Expenses + Other Income/Expenses - Taxes

@EXAMPLE_EXTRACTION
Example of how to extract and format data from this document:

```python
# Extract revenue information for specific period with hierarchy awareness
def extract_revenue(document, context_code):
    # Find the Revenue section
    revenue_section = find_section(document, '<Revenue>')

    # Extract all line items with their context codes
    revenue_data = {}
    totals = {}
    parent_child_map = {}

    # First pass: collect all items and identify parent-child relationships
    for line in revenue_section:
        if context_code in line.split('|')[1].strip():
            columns = line.split('|')
            raw_item_name = columns[0].strip()

            # Parse hierarchy information
            if raw_item_name.startswith('@TOTAL:'):
                # This is a total item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@TOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 0  # Top level
            elif raw_item_name.startswith('@SUBTOTAL:'):
                # This is a subtotal item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@SUBTOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 1  # Mid level
            elif '@CHILD_OF:' in raw_item_name:
                # This is a child item, extract its parent
                parts = raw_item_name.split('@CHILD_OF:')
                item_name = parts[0].replace('↳', '').strip()
                parent_name = parts[1].strip()
                parent_child_map[item_name] = parent_name
                is_total = False
                level = 2  # Child level
            else:
                # Regular item
                item_name = raw_item_name.strip()
                is_total = False
                level = 1  # Base level

            # Find the value corresponding to the context code
            value = get_value_for_context(columns, context_code)

            # Store with hierarchy information
            if is_total:
                totals[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'components': []  # Will be filled in second pass
                }
            else:
                revenue_data[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'parent': parent_child_map.get(item_name)
                }

    # Second pass: associate children with their parent totals
    for item_name, item_data in revenue_data.items():
        parent = item_data.get('parent')
        if parent and parent in totals:
            totals[parent]['components'].append(item_name)

    # Combine the data structures
    result = {
        'line_items': revenue_data,
        'totals': totals,
        # Include verification formulas
        'verify': {
            'sum_components': 'Sum of all components should equal the total',
            'formula': 'Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue + Other_Revenue'
        }
    }
    return result
```

Example hierarchical data format for extraction:

```json
{
  "line_items": {
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Service_Revenue": {
      "value": 16320,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Automotive_Revenue": {
      "value": 52300,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    },
    "Energy_Revenue": {
      "value": 20180,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    }
  },
  "totals": {
    "Total_Revenue": {
      "value": 88800,
      "level": 0,
      "components": ["Product_Revenue", "Service_Revenue"],
      "contexts": {
        "c-1": 88800,           // Using short code
        "FY2023": 88800,        // Using semantic code
        "Consolidated_2023": 88800  // Using segment information
      }
    },
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "components": ["Automotive_Revenue", "Energy_Revenue"]
    }
  },
  "verify": {
    "equations": [
      "Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue",
      "Product_Revenue = Automotive_Revenue + Energy_Revenue"
    ],
    "verified": true
  },
  "metadata": {
    "statement_type": "Income_Statement",
    "period": "FY2023",
    "hierarchical": true
  }
}
```

Note: This hierarchical structure makes parent-child relationships explicit, enabling accurate calculation and validation of totals. The hierarchy levels indicate:
- Level 0: Main totals (like Total Revenue)
- Level 1: Major categories (like Product Revenue)
- Level 2: Subcategories (like Automotive Revenue)

You can use either the numeric short codes (c-1, c-2) or the semantic codes (FY2023, BS_2023_12_31) to access context values. The semantic codes are more descriptive and self-explanatory.
